title="This is a featured article. srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/30px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/40px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>\n     </a>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    Radiocarbon dating\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a href="#mw-head">\n      navigation\n     </a>\n     ,\n     <a href="#p-search">\n      search\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">\n     <div class="mw-parser-output">\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Radiocarbon dating\n       </b>\n       (also referred to as\n       <b>\n        carbon dating\n       </b>\n       or\n       <b>\n        carbon-14 dating\n       </b>\n       ) is a method for\n       <a href="/wiki/Chronological_dating" title="Chronological dating">\n        determining the age\n       </a>\n       of an object containing\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organic_material" title="Organic material">\n        organic material\n       </a>\n       by using the properties of\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon-14" title="Carbon-14">\n        radiocarbon\n       </a>\n       (\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ), a radioactive\n       <a href="/wiki/Isotopes_of_carbon" title="Isotopes of carbon">\n        isotope of carbon\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The method was developed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Willard_Libby" title="Willard Libby">\n        Willard Libby\n       </a>\n       in the late 1940s and soon became a standard tool for archaeologists. Libby received the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">\n        Nobel Prize in Chemistry\n       </a>\n       for his work in 1960. The radiocarbon dating method is based on the fact that radiocarbon is constantly being created in the atmosphere by the interaction of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">\n        cosmic rays\n       </a>\n       with atmospheric\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">\n        nitrogen\n       </a>\n       . The resulting radiocarbon combines with atmospheric\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">\n        oxygen\n       </a>\n       to form radioactive\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       , which is incorporated into plants by\n       <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">\n        photosynthesis\n       </a>\n       ; animals then acquire\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       by eating the plants. When the animal or plant dies, it stops exchanging carbon with its environment, and from that point onwards the amount of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       it contains begins to decrease as the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       undergoes\n       <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_decay" title="Radioactive decay">\n        radioactive decay\n       </a>\n       . Measuring the amount of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in a sample from a dead plant or animal such as a piece of wood or a fragment of bone provides information that can be used to calculate when the animal or plant died. The older a sample is, the less\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       there is to be detected, and because the\n       <a href="/wiki/Half-life" title="Half-life">\n        half-life\n       </a>\n       of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       (the period of time after which half of a given sample will have decayed) is about 5,730 years, the oldest dates that can be reliably measured by this process date to around 50,000 years ago, although special preparation methods occasionally permit accurate analysis of older samples.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The idea behind radiocarbon dating is straightforward, but years of work were required to develop the technique to the point where accurate dates could be obtained. Research has been ongoing since the 1960s to determine what the proportion of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere has been over the past fifty thousand years. The resulting data, in the form of a calibration curve, is now used to convert a given measurement of radiocarbon in a sample into an estimate of the sample\'s calendar age. Other corrections must be made to account for the proportion of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in different types of organisms (fractionation), and the varying levels of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       throughout the\n       <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">\n        biosphere\n       </a>\n       (reservoir effects). Additional complications come from the burning of fossil fuels such as coal and oil, and from the above-ground nuclear tests done in the 1950s and 1960s. Because the time it takes to convert biological materials to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" title="Fossil fuels">\n        fossil fuels\n       </a>\n       is substantially longer than the time it takes for its\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       to decay below detectable levels, fossil fuels contain almost no\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , and as a result there was a noticeable drop in the proportion of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere beginning in the late 19th century. Conversely, nuclear testing increased the amount of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere, which attained a maximum in 1963 of almost twice what it had been before the testing began.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Measurement of radiocarbon was originally done by beta-counting devices, which counted the amount of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beta_radiation" title="Beta radiation">\n        beta radiation\n       </a>\n       emitted by decaying\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       atoms in a sample. More recently,\n       <a href="/wiki/Accelerator_mass_spectrometry" title="Accelerator mass spectrometry">\n        accelerator mass spectrometry\n       </a>\n       has become the method of choice; it counts all the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       atoms in the sample and not just the few that happen to decay during the measurements; it can therefore be used with much smaller samples (as small as individual plant seeds), and gives results much more quickly. The development of radiocarbon dating has had a profound impact on\n       <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">\n        archaeology\n       </a>\n       . In addition to permitting more accurate dating within archaeological sites than previous methods, it allows comparison of dates of events across great distances. Histories of archaeology often refer to its impact as the "radiocarbon revolution". Radiocarbon dating has allowed key transitions in prehistory to be dated, such as the end of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Younger_Dryas" title="Younger Dryas">\n        last ice age\n       </a>\n       , and the beginning of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">\n        Neolithic\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">\n        Bronze Age\n       </a>\n       in different regions.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n href="#Pleistocene.2FHolocene_boundary_in_Two_Creeks_Fossil_Forest">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.2.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Pleistocene/Holocene boundary in Two Creeks Fossil Forest\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-25">\n             <a href="#Dead_Sea_Scrolls">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.2.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Dead Sea Scrolls\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Impact">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Impact\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28">\n         <a href="#Notes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#Sources">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Sources\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Background">\n        Background\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 1939,\n       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Kamen" title="Martin Kamen">\n        Martin Kamen\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Ruben" title="Samuel Ruben">\n        Samuel Ruben\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lawrence_Radiation_Laboratory" title="Lawrence Radiation Laboratory">\n        Radiation Laboratory at Berkeley\n       </a>\n       began experiments to determine if any of the elements common in organic matter had isotopes with half-lives long enough to be of value in biomedical research. They synthesized\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       using the laboratory\'s cyclotron accelerator and soon discovered that the atom\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Half-life" title="Half-life">\n        half-life\n       </a>\n       was far longer than had been previously thought.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:20_1-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:20-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This was followed by a prediction by\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Serge_A._Korff&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Serge A. Korff (page does not exist)">\n        Serge A. Korff\n       </a>\n       , then employed at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Institute" title="Franklin Institute">\n        Franklin Institute\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       , that the interaction of slow neutrons with\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        N\n       </span>\n       in the upper atmosphere would create\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taylor269_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-taylor269-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It had previously been thought that\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       would be more likely to be created by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deuteron" title="Deuteron">\n        deuterons\n       </a>\n       interacting with\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:20_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:20-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At some time during World War II,\n       <a href="/wiki/Willard_Libby" title="Willard Libby">\n        Willard Libby\n       </a>\n       , who was then at Berkeley, learned of Korff\'s research and conceived the idea that it might be possible to use radiocarbon for dating.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taylor269_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-taylor269-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1945, Libby moved to the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">\n        University of Chicago\n       </a>\n       where he began his work on radiocarbon dating. He published a paper in 1946 in which he proposed that the carbon in living matter might include\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       as well as non-radioactive carbon.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Libby and several collaborators proceeded to experiment with\n       <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">\n        methane\n       </a>\n       collected from sewage works in Baltimore, and after\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isotope_enrichment" title="Isotope enrichment">\n        isotopically enriching\n       </a>\n       their samples they were able to demonstrate that they contained radioactive\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       . By contrast, methane created from petroleum showed no radiocarbon activity because of its age. The results were summarized in a paper in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">\n         Science\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       in 1947, in which the authors commented that their results implied it would be possible to date materials containing carbon of organic origin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson_1947_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Anderson_1947-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Libby and\n       <a href="/wiki/James_R._Arnold" title="James R. Arnold">\n        James Arnold\n       </a>\n       proceeded to test the radiocarbon dating theory by analyzing samples with known ages. For example, two samples taken from the tombs of two Egyptian kings,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoser" title="Zoser">\n        Zoser\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sneferu" title="Sneferu">\n        Sneferu\n       </a>\n       , independently dated to 2625 BC plus or minus 75 years, were dated by radiocarbon measurement to an average of 2800 BC plus or minus 250 years. These results were published in\n       <i>\n        Science\n       </i>\n       in 1949.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-libby49_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-libby49-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_60-61_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_60-61-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Within 11 years of their announcement, more than 20 radiocarbon dating laboratories had been set up worldwide.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1960, Libby was awarded the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">\n        Nobel Prize in Chemistry\n       </a>\n       for this work.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_and_chemical_details">\n        Physical and chemical details\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Physical and chemical details">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon-14" title="Carbon-14">\n        Carbon-14\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In nature,\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">\n        carbon\n       </a>\n       exists as two stable, nonradioactive\n       <a href="/wiki/Isotope" title="Isotope">\n        isotopes\n       </a>\n       :\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon-12" title="Carbon-12">\n        carbon-12\n       </a>\n       (\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon-13" title="Carbon-13">\n        carbon-13\n       </a>\n       (\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ), and a radioactive isotope,\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon-14" title="Carbon-14">\n        carbon-14\n       </a>\n       (\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ), also known as "radiocarbon". The half-life of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       (the time it takes for half of a given amount of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_decay" title="Radioactive decay">\n        decay\n       </a>\n       ) is about 5,730 years, so its concentration in the atmosphere might be expected to reduce over thousands of years, but\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is constantly being produced in the lower\n       <a href="/wiki/Stratosphere" title="Stratosphere">\n        stratosphere\n       </a>\n       and upper\n       <a href="/wiki/Troposphere" title="Troposphere">\n        troposphere\n       </a>\n       by\n       <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">\n        cosmic rays\n       </a>\n       , which generate neutrons that in turn create\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       when they strike\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nitrogen-14" title="Nitrogen-14">\n        nitrogen-14\n       </a>\n       (\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        N\n       </span>\n       ) atoms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The following\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reaction" title="Nuclear reaction">\n        nuclear reaction\n       </a>\n       creates\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        n +\n        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">\n          14\n          <br/>\n          7\n         </span>\n         N\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">\n          14\n          <br/>\n          6\n         </span>\n         C\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + p\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where n represents a\n       <a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">\n        neutron\n       </a>\n       and p represents a\n       <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">\n        proton\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CES_476_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CES_476-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Once produced, the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       quickly combines with the oxygen in the atmosphere to form carbon dioxide (\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ). Carbon dioxide produced in this way diffuses in the atmosphere, is dissolved in the ocean, and is taken up by plants via\n       <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">\n        photosynthesis\n       </a>\n       . Animals eat the plants, and ultimately the radiocarbon is distributed throughout the\n       <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">\n        biosphere\n       </a>\n       . The ratio of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       to\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is approximately 1.5 parts of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       to 10\n       <sup>\n        12\n       </sup>\n       parts of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_56-58_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_56-58-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition, about 1% of the carbon atoms are of the stable isotope\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The equation for the radioactive decay of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Currie_2004_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Currie_2004-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">\n          14\n          <br/>\n          6\n         </span>\n         C\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">\n          14\n          <br/>\n          7\n         </span>\n         N\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        +\n        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n         e\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          \xe2\x88\x92\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        +\n        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n         <span style="text-decoration:overline;">\n          \xce\xbd\n         </span>\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          e\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       By emitting a beta particle (an\n       <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">\n        electron\n       </a>\n       , e\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x92\n       </sup>\n       ) and an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antineutrino" title="Antineutrino">\n        electron antineutrino\n       </a>\n       (\n       <span style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        <span style="text-decoration:overline;">\n         \xce\xbd\n        </span>\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         e\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ), one of the neutrons in the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       nucleus changes to a proton and the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       nucleus reverts to the stable (non-radioactive) isotope\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        N\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Principles">\n        Principles\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Principles">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       During its life, a plant or animal is exchanging carbon with its surroundings, so the carbon it contains will have the same proportion of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       as the atmosphere. Once it dies, it ceases to acquire\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , but the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       within its biological material at that time will continue to decay, and so the ratio of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       to\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in its remains will gradually decrease. Because\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       decays at a known rate, the proportion of radiocarbon can be used to determine how long it has been since a given sample stopped exchanging carbon\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 the older the sample, the less\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       will be left.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_56-58_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_56-58-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The equation governing the decay of a radioactive isotope is:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               N\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                N\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 0\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                e\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mo>\n                 \xe2\x88\x92\n                 <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n                </mo>\n                <mi>\n                 \xce\xbb\n                 <!-- \xce\xbb -->\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 t\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle N=N_{0}e^{-\\lambda t}\\,}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="N=N_{0}e^{-\\lambda t}\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b7fdc3b28d21a0ea7faab8a2e3d185d1ea91d01a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.687ex; height:3.009ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where\n       <i>\n        N\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        0\n       </sub>\n       is the number of atoms of the isotope in the original sample (at time\n       <i>\n        t\n       </i>\n       = 0, when the organism from which the sample was taken died), and\n       <i>\n        N\n       </i>\n       is the number of atoms left after time\n       <i>\n        t\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        \xce\xbb\n       </i>\n       is a constant that depends on the particular isotope; for a given isotope it is equal to the reciprocal of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_decay#Time_constant_and_mean-life" title="Radioactive decay">\n        mean-life\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 i.e. the average or expected time a given atom will survive before undergoing radioactive decay.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The mean-life, denoted by\n       <i>\n        \xcf\x84\n       </i>\n       , of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is 8,267 years, so the equation above can be rewritten as:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               t\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mn>\n               8267\n              </mn>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x8b\x85\n               <!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               ln\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x81\xa1\n               <!-- \xe2\x81\xa1 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                N\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 0\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mo>\n                /\n               </mo>\n              </mrow>\n              <mi>\n               N\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mtext>\n                years\n               </mtext>\n              </mrow>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle t=8267\\cdot \\ln(N_{0}/N){\\text{ years}}}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle t=8267\\cdot \\ln(N_{0}/N){\\text{ years}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/312bd1faeb68359c7ede67e8a25fa6ec3f27af1b" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:26.199ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The sample is assumed to have originally had the same\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio as the ratio in the atmosphere, and since the size of the sample is known, the total number of atoms in the sample can be calculated, yielding\n       <i>\n        N\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        0\n       </sub>\n       , the number of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       atoms in the original sample. Measurement of\n       <i>\n        N\n       </i>\n       , the number of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       atoms currently in the sample, allows the calculation of\n       <i>\n        t\n       </i>\n       , the age of the sample, using the equation above.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_56-58_12-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_56-58-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The half-life of a radioactive isotope (usually denoted by t\n       <sub>\n        1/2\n       </sub>\n       ) is a more familiar concept than the mean-life, so although the equations above are expressed in terms of the mean-life, it is more usual to quote the value of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       \'s half-life than its mean-life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [note 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The currently accepted value for the half-life of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is 5,730 years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This means that after 5,730 years, only half of the initial\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       will remain; a quarter will remain after 11,460 years; an eighth after 17,190 years; and so on.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The above calculations make several assumptions, such as that the level of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere has remained constant over time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In fact, the level of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere has varied significantly and as a result the values provided by the equation above have to be corrected by using data from other sources.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_.281990.29_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_.281990.29-17">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is done by calibration curves, which convert a measurement of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in a sample into an estimated calendar age. The calculations involve several steps and include an intermediate value called the "radiocarbon age", which is the age in "radiocarbon years" of the sample: an age quoted in radiocarbon years means that no calibration curve has been used \xe2\x88\x92 the calculations for radiocarbon years assume that the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio has not changed over time. Calculating radiocarbon ages also requires the value of the half-life for\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , which for more than a decade after Libby\'s initial work was thought to be 5,568 years. This was revised in the early 1960s to 5,730 years, which meant that many calculated dates in papers published prior to this were incorrect (the error in the half-life is about 3%). For consistency with these early papers, and to avoid the risk of a double correction for the incorrect half-life, radiocarbon ages are still calculated using the incorrect half-life value. A correction for the half-life is incorporated into calibration curves, so even though radiocarbon ages are calculated using a half-life value that is known to be incorrect, the final reported calibrated date, in calendar years, is accurate. When a date is quoted, the reader should be aware that if it is an uncalibrated date (a term used for dates given in radiocarbon years) it may differ substantially from the best estimate of the actual calendar date, both because it uses the wrong value for the half-life of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , and because no correction (calibration) has been applied for the historical variation of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere over time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:12-18">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [note 2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Carbon_exchange_reservoir">\n        Carbon exchange reservoir\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Carbon exchange reservoir">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carbon_exchange_reservoir_2.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="612" height="410" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Carbon_exchange_reservoir_2.svg/400px-Carbon_exchange_reservoir_2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Carbon_exchange_reservoir_2.svg/600px-Carbon_exchange_reservoir_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Carbon_exchange_reservoir_2.svg/800px-Carbon_exchange_reservoir_2.svg.png 2x" width="400"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carbon_exchange_reservoir_2.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Simplified version of the carbon exchange reservoir, showing proportions of carbon and relative activity of the\n         <span class="chemf nowrap">\n          <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n           14\n           <br/>\n          </span>\n          C\n         </span>\n         in each reservoir\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-11">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n           [5]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n          <a href="#cite_note-23">\n           [note 3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Carbon is distributed throughout the atmosphere, the biosphere, and the oceans; these are referred to collectively as the carbon exchange reservoir,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and each component is also referred to individually as a carbon exchange reservoir. The different elements of the carbon exchange reservoir vary in how much carbon they store, and in how long it takes for the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       generated by cosmic rays to fully mix with them. This affects the ratio of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       to\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the different reservoirs, and hence the radiocarbon ages of samples that originated in each reservoir.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The atmosphere, which is where\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is generated, contains about 1.9% of the total carbon in the reservoirs, and the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       it contains mixes in less than seven years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GC_128-9_22-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GC_128-9-22">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Warneck_690_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Warneck_690-25">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The ratio of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       to\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere is taken as the baseline for the other reservoirs: if another reservoir has a lower ratio of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       to\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , it indicates that the carbon is older and hence that some of the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       has decayed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_.281990.29_17-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_.281990.29-17">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The ocean surface is an example: it contains 2.4% of the carbon in the exchange reservoir,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GC_128-9_22-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GC_128-9-22">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but there is only about 95% as much\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       as would be expected if the ratio were the same as in the atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The time it takes for carbon from the atmosphere to mix with the surface ocean is only a few years,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but the surface waters also receive water from the deep ocean, which has more than 90% of the carbon in the reservoir.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_.281990.29_17-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_.281990.29-17">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Water in the deep ocean takes about 1,000 years to circulate back through surface waters, and so the surface waters contain a combination of older water, with depleted\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , and water recently at the surface, with\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in equilibrium with the atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_.281990.29_17-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_.281990.29-17">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Creatures living at the ocean surface have the same\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratios as the water they live in, and as a result of the reduced\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio, the radiocarbon age of marine life is typically about 440 years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman1995_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman1995-27">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cronin2010_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cronin2010-28">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [note 4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Organisms on land are in closer equilibrium with the atmosphere and have the same\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio as the atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These organisms contain about 1.3% of the carbon in the reservoir; sea organisms have a mass of less than 1% of those on land and are not shown on the diagram.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GC_128-9_22-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GC_128-9-22">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Accumulated dead organic matter, of both plants and animals, exceeds the mass of the biosphere by a factor of nearly 3, and since this matter is no longer exchanging carbon with its environment, it has a\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio lower than that of the biosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_9-15_5-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_9-15-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dating_considerations">\n        Dating considerations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Dating considerations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating_considerations" title="Radiocarbon dating considerations">\n        Radiocarbon dating considerations\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The variation in the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio in different parts of the carbon exchange reservoir means that a straightforward calculation of the age of a sample based on the amount of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       it contains will often give an incorrect result. There are several other possible sources of error that need to be considered. The errors are of four general types:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        variations in the\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          14\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n         C\n        </span>\n        /\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          12\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n         C\n        </span>\n        ratio in the atmosphere, both geographically and over time;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        isotopic fractionation;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        variations in the\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          14\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n         C\n        </span>\n        /\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          12\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n         C\n        </span>\n        ratio in different parts of the reservoir;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        contamination.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Atmospheric_variation">\n        Atmospheric variation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Atmospheric variation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In the early years of using the technique, it was understood that it depended on the atmospheric\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio having remained the same over the preceding few thousand years. To verify the accuracy of the method, several artefacts that were datable by other techniques were tested; the results of the testing were in reasonable agreement with the true ages of the objects. Over time, however, discrepancies began to appear between the known chronology for the oldest Egyptian dynasties and the radiocarbon dates of Egyptian artefacts. Neither the pre-existing Egyptian chronology nor the new radiocarbon dating method could be assumed to be accurate, but a third possibility was that the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio had changed over time. The question was resolved by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dendrochronology" title="Dendrochronology">\n        study of tree rings\n       </a>\n       :\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_16-20_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_16-20-30">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Suess_1970_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Suess_1970-31">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor_.26_Bar-Yosef_.282014.29_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Taylor_.26_Bar-Yosef_.282014.29-32">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       comparison of overlapping series of tree rings allowed the construction of a continuous sequence of tree-ring data that spanned 8,000 years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_16-20_30-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_16-20-30">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (Since that time the tree-ring data series has been extended to 13,900 years.)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INTCAL13_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-INTCAL13-33">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the 1960s,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hans_Suess" title="Hans Suess">\n        Hans Suess\n       </a>\n       was able to use the tree-ring sequence to show that the dates derived from radiocarbon were consistent with the dates assigned by Egyptologists. This was possible because although annual plants, such as corn, have a\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio that reflects the atmospheric ratio at the time they were growing, trees only add material to their outermost tree ring in any given year, while the inner tree rings don\'t get their\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       replenished and instead start losing\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       through decay. Hence each ring preserves a record of the atmospheric\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio of the year it grew in. Carbon-dating the wood from the tree rings themselves provides the check needed on the atmospheric\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio: with a sample of known date, and a measurement of the value of\n       <i>\n        N\n       </i>\n       (the number of atoms of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       remaining in the sample), the carbon-dating equation allows the calculation of\n       <i>\n        N\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        0\n       </sub>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 the number of atoms of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the sample at the time the tree ring was formed \xe2\x80\x93 and hence the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio in the atmosphere at that time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_16-20_30-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_16-20-30">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor_.26_Bar-Yosef_.282014.29_32-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Taylor_.26_Bar-Yosef_.282014.29-32">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Equipped with the results of carbon-dating the tree rings, it became possible to construct calibration curves designed to correct the errors caused by the variation over time in the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:18_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:18-34">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These curves are described in more detail\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating#Calibration" title="Radiocarbon dating">\n        below\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Radiocarbon_bomb_spike.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="600" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Radiocarbon_bomb_spike.svg/300px-Radiocarbon_bomb_spike.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Radiocarbon_bomb_spike.svg/450px-Radiocarbon_bomb_spike.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Radiocarbon_bomb_spike.svg/600px-Radiocarbon_bomb_spike.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Radiocarbon_bomb_spike.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Atmospheric\n         <span class="chemf nowrap">\n          <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n           14\n           <br/>\n          </span>\n          C\n         </span>\n         , New Zealand\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n          <a href="#cite_note-35">\n           [31]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         and Austria.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n          <a href="#cite_note-36">\n           [32]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         The New Zealand curve is representative of the Southern Hemisphere; the Austrian curve is representative of the Northern Hemisphere. Atmospheric nuclear weapon tests almost doubled the concentration of\n         <span class="chemf nowrap">\n          <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n           14\n           <br/>\n          </span>\n          C\n         </span>\n         in the Northern Hemisphere.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Currie_2004_13-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Currie_2004-13">\n           [13]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         The date that the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partial_Test_Ban_Treaty" title="Partial Test Ban Treaty">\n          Partial Test Ban Treaty\n         </a>\n         (PTBT) went into effect is marked on the graph.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Coal and oil began to be burned in large quantities during the 19th century.
