Both are sufficiently old that they contain little detectable\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       and, as a result, the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       released substantially diluted the atmospheric\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio. Dating an object from the early 20th century hence gives an apparent date older than the true date. For the same reason,\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       concentrations in the neighbourhood of large cities are lower than the atmospheric average. This fossil fuel effect (also known as the Suess effect, after Hans Suess, who first reported it in 1955) would only amount to a reduction of 0.2% in\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       activity if the additional carbon from fossil fuels were distributed throughout the carbon exchange reservoir, but because of the long delay in mixing with the deep ocean, the actual effect is a 3% reduction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_16-20_30-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_16-20-30">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_71-72_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_71-72-37">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A much larger effect comes from above-ground nuclear testing, which released large numbers of neutrons and created\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       . From about 1950 until 1963, when atmospheric nuclear testing was banned, it is estimated that several tonnes of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       were created. If all this extra\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       had immediately been spread across the entire carbon exchange reservoir, it would have led to an increase in the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio of only a few per cent, but the immediate effect was to almost double the amount of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere, with the peak level occurring in about 1965. The level has since dropped, as this\n       <a href="/wiki/Bomb_pulse" title="Bomb pulse">\n        bomb pulse\n       </a>\n       or "bomb carbon" (as it is sometimes called) percolates into the rest of the reservoir.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_16-20_30-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_16-20-30">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_71-72_37-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_71-72-37">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PTBT_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PTBT-38">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Isotopic_fractionation">\n        Isotopic fractionation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Isotopic fractionation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Photosynthesis is the primary process by which carbon moves from the atmosphere into living things. In photosynthetic pathways\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is absorbed slightly more easily than\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , which in turn is more easily absorbed than\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       . The differential uptake of the three carbon isotopes leads to\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratios in plants that differ from the ratios in the atmosphere. This effect is known as isotopic fractionation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_20-23_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_20-23-39">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leng_246_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Leng_246-40">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       To determine the degree of fractionation that takes place in a given plant, the amounts of both\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       isotopes are measured, and the resulting\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio is then compared to a standard ratio known as PDB.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [note 5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio is used instead of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       because the former is much easier to measure, and the latter can be easily derived: the depletion of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       relative to\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is proportional to the difference in the atomic masses of the two isotopes, so the depletion for\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is twice the depletion of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_.281990.29_17-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_.281990.29-17">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The fractionation of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , known as\n       <a href="/wiki/%CE%9413C" title="\xce\x9413C">\n        <span class="texhtml">\n         \xce\xb4\n        </span>\n        <sup>\n         13\n        </sup>\n        C\n       </a>\n       , is calculated as follows:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_20-23_39-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_20-23-39">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display:        </mrow>\n                    </msup>\n                    <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                     C\n                    </mi>\n                   </mrow>\n                  </mfrac>\n            <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mn>\n               1\n              </mn>\n              <mrow </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where the \xe2\x80\xb0 sign indicates\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parts_per_thousand" title="Parts per thousand">\n        parts per thousand\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_20-23_39-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_20-23-39">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Because the PDB standard contains an unusually high proportion of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [note 6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       most measured\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        \xce\xb4\n       </span>\n       <sup>\n        13\n       </sup>\n       C values are negative.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NR_sheep.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/NR_sheep.jpg/300px-NR_sheep.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/NR_sheep.jpg/450px-NR_sheep.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/NR_sheep.jpg/600px-NR_sheep.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NR_sheep.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/North_Ronaldsay_sheep" title="North Ronaldsay sheep">\n          North Ronaldsay sheep\n         </a>\n         on the beach in\n         <a href="/wiki/North_Ronaldsay" title="North Ronaldsay">\n          North Ronaldsay\n         </a>\n         . In the winter, these sheep eat seaweed, which has a higher\n         <span class="texhtml">\n          \xce\xb4\n         </span>\n         <sup>\n          13\n         </sup>\n         C content than grass; samples from these sheep have a\n         <span class="texhtml">\n          \xce\xb4\n         </span>\n         <sup>\n          13\n         </sup>\n         C value of about \xe2\x88\x9213\xe2\x80\xb0, which is much higher than for sheep that feed on grasses.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_20-23_39-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_20-23-39">\n           [35]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-left: 2em; text-align: center; float: right">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Material\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Typical\n         <span class="texhtml">\n          \xce\xb4\n         </span>\n         <sup>\n          13\n         </sup>\n         C range\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         PDB\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0\xe2\x80\xb0\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Marine plankton\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x88\x9222\xe2\x80\xb0 to \xe2\x88\x9217\xe2\x80\xb0\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leng_246_40-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Leng_246-40">\n           [36]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         C3 plants\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x88\x9230\xe2\x80\xb0 to \xe2\x88\x9222\xe2\x80\xb0\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leng_246_40-2">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Leng_246-40">\n           [36]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         C4 plants\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x88\x9215\xe2\x80\xb0 to \xe2\x88\x929\xe2\x80\xb0\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leng_246_40-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Leng_246-40">\n           [36]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Atmospheric\n         <span class="chemf nowrap">\n          CO\n          <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n           <br/>\n           2\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x88\x928\xe2\x80\xb0\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_20-23_39-4">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_20-23-39">\n           [35]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Marine\n         <span class="chemf nowrap">\n          CO\n          <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n           <br/>\n           2\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x88\x9232\xe2\x80\xb0 to \xe2\x88\x9213\xe2\x80\xb0\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leng_246_40-4">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Leng_246-40">\n           [36]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       For marine organisms, the details of the photosynthesis reactions are less well understood, and the\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        \xce\xb4\n       </span>\n       <sup>\n        13\n       </sup>\n       C values for marine photosynthetic organisms are dependent on temperature. At higher temperatures,\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       has poor solubility in water, which means there is less\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       available for the photosynthetic reactions. Under these conditions, fractionation is reduced, and at temperatures above 14\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C the\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        \xce\xb4\n       </span>\n       <sup>\n        13\n       </sup>\n       C values are correspondingly higher, while at lower temperatures,\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       becomes more soluble and hence more available to marine organisms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leng_246_40-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Leng_246-40">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        \xce\xb4\n       </span>\n       <sup>\n        13\n       </sup>\n       C value for animals depends on their diet. An animal that eats food with high\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        \xce\xb4\n       </span>\n       <sup>\n        13\n       </sup>\n       C values will have a higher\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        \xce\xb4\n       </span>\n       <sup>\n        13\n       </sup>\n       C than one that eats food with lower\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        \xce\xb4\n       </span>\n       <sup>\n        13\n       </sup>\n       C values.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_20-23_39-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_20-23-39">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The animal\'s own biochemical processes can also impact the results: for example, both bone minerals and bone collagen typically have a higher concentration of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       than is found in the animal\'s diet, though for different biochemical reasons. The enrichment of bone\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       also implies that excreted material is depleted in\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       relative to the diet.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       makes up about 1% of the carbon in a sample, the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio can be accurately measured by\n       <a href="/wiki/Mass_spectrometry" title="Mass spectrometry">\n        mass spectrometry\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_.281990.29_17-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_.281990.29-17">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Typical values of\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        \xce\xb4\n       </span>\n       <sup>\n        13\n       </sup>\n       C have been found by experiment for many plants, as well as for different parts of animals such as bone\n       <a href="/wiki/Collagen" title="Collagen">\n        collagen\n       </a>\n       , but when dating a given sample it is better to determine the\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        \xce\xb4\n       </span>\n       <sup>\n        13\n       </sup>\n       C value for that sample directly than to rely on the published values.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_20-23_39-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_20-23-39">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The carbon exchange between atmospheric\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       and carbonate at the ocean surface is also subject to fractionation, with\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere more likely than\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       to dissolve in the ocean. The result is an overall increase in the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio in the ocean of 1.5%, relative to the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio in the atmosphere. This increase in\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       concentration almost exactly cancels out the decrease caused by the upwelling of water (containing old, and hence\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       depleted, carbon) from the deep ocean, so that direct measurements of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       radiation are similar to measurements for the rest of the biosphere. Correcting for isotopic fractionation, as is done for all radiocarbon dates to allow comparison between results from different parts of the biosphere, gives an apparent age of about 440 years for ocean surface water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_.281990.29_17-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_.281990.29-17">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cronin2010_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cronin2010-28">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reservoir_effects">\n        Reservoir effects\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Reservoir effects">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Libby\'s original exchange reservoir hypothesis assumed that the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio in the exchange reservoir is constant all over the world,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Libby1965_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Libby1965-46">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but it has since been discovered that there are several causes of variation in the ratio across the reservoir.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman1995_27-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman1995-27">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Marine effect\n       </b>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       in the atmosphere transfers to the ocean by dissolving in the surface water as carbonate and bicarbonate ions; at the same time the carbonate ions in the water are returning to the air as\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Libby1965_46-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Libby1965-46">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This exchange process brings\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       from the atmosphere into the surface waters of the ocean, but the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       thus introduced takes a long time to percolate through the entire volume of the ocean. The deepest parts of the ocean mix very slowly with the surface waters, and the mixing is uneven. The main mechanism that brings deep water to the surface is upwelling, which is more common in regions closer to the equator. Upwelling is also influenced by factors such as the topography of the local ocean bottom and coastlines, the climate, and wind patterns. Overall, the mixing of deep and surface waters takes far longer than the mixing of atmospheric\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       with the surface waters, and as a result water from some deep ocean areas has an apparent radiocarbon age of several thousand years. Upwelling mixes this "old" water with the surface water, giving the surface water an apparent age of about several hundred years (after correcting for fractionation).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman1995_27-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman1995-27">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This effect is not uniform\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 the average effect is about 440 years, but there are local deviations of several hundred years for areas that are geographically close to each other.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman1995_27-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman1995-27">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cronin2010_28-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cronin2010-28">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The effect also applies to marine organisms such as shells, and marine mammals such as whales and seals, which have radiocarbon ages that appear to be hundreds of years old.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman1995_27-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman1995-27">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Hemisphere effect\n       </b>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The northern and southern hemispheres have\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_circulation" title="Atmospheric circulation">\n        atmospheric circulation\n       </a>\n       systems that are sufficiently independent of each other that there is a noticeable time lag in mixing between the two. The atmospheric\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio is lower in the southern hemisphere, with an apparent additional age of 30 years for radiocarbon results from the south as compared to the north. This is probably because the greater surface area of ocean in the southern hemisphere means that there is more carbon exchanged between the ocean and the atmosphere than in the north. Since the surface ocean is depleted in\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       because of the marine effect,\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       is removed from the southern atmosphere more quickly than in the north.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman1995_27-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman1995-27">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Other effects\n       </b>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       If the carbon in freshwater is partly acquired from aged carbon, such as rocks, then the result will be a reduction in the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio in the water. For example, rivers that pass over\n       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">\n        limestone\n       </a>\n       , which is mostly composed of\n       <a href="/wiki/Calcium_carbonate" title="Calcium carbonate">\n        calcium carbonate\n       </a>\n       , will acquire carbonate ions. Similarly, groundwater can contain carbon derived from the rocks through which it has passed. These rocks are usually so old that they no longer contain any measurable\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , so this carbon lowers the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio of the water it enters, which can lead to apparent ages of thousands of years for both the affected water and the plants and freshwater organisms that live in it.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_.281990.29_17-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_.281990.29-17">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hard_water" title="Hard water">\n        hard water\n       </a>\n       effect because it is often associated with calcium ions, which are characteristic of hard water; other sources of carbon such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Humus" title="Humus">\n        humus\n       </a>\n       can produce similar results.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman1995_27-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman1995-27">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The effect varies greatly and there is no general offset that can be applied; additional research is usually needed to determine the size of the offset, for example by comparing the radiocarbon age of deposited freshwater shells with associated organic material.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanic_eruptions" title="Volcanic eruptions">\n        Volcanic eruptions\n       </a>\n       eject large amounts of carbon into the air. The carbon is of geological origin and has no detectable\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , so the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio in the vicinity of the volcano is depressed relative to surrounding areas. Dormant volcanoes can also emit aged carbon. Plants that photosynthesize this carbon also have lower\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratios: for example, plants on the Greek island of\n       <a href="/wiki/Santorini" title="Santorini">\n        Santorini\n       </a>\n       , near the volcano, have apparent ages of up to a thousand years. These effects are hard to predict\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 the town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_(Santorini)" title="Akrotiri (Santorini)">\n        Akrotiri\n       </a>\n       , on Santorini, was destroyed in a volcanic eruption thousands of years ago, but radiocarbon dates for objects recovered from the ruins of the town show surprisingly close agreement with dates derived from other means. If the dates for Akrotiri are confirmed, it would indicate that the volcanic effect in this case was minimal.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman1995_27-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman1995-27">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contamination">\n        Contamination\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Contamination">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Any addition of carbon to a sample of a different age will cause the measured date to be inaccurate. Contamination with modern carbon causes a sample to appear to be younger than it really is: the effect is greater for older samples. If a sample that is 17,000 years old is contaminated so that 1% of the sample is modern carbon, it will appear to be 600 years younger; for a sample that is 34,000 years old the same amount of contamination would cause an error of 4,000 years. Contamination with old carbon, with no remaining\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , causes an error in the other direction independent of age\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 a sample contaminated with 1% old carbon will appear to be about 80 years older than it really is, regardless of the date of the sample.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Samples">\n        Samples\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Samples">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating_samples" title="Radiocarbon dating samples">\n        Radiocarbon dating samples\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Samples for dating need to be converted into a form suitable for measuring the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       content; this can mean conversion to gaseous, liquid, or solid form, depending on the measurement technique to be used. Before this can be done, the sample must be treated to remove any contamination and any unwanted constituents.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_27-30_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_27-30-49">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This includes removing visible contaminants, such as rootlets that may have penetrated the sample since its burial.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_27-30_49-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_27-30-49">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Alkali and acid washes can be used to remove humic acid and carbonate contamination, but care has to be taken to avoid destroying or damaging the sample.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AitkenWashing_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AitkenWashing-50">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Material_considerations">\n        Material considerations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Material considerations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        It is common to reduce a wood sample to just the cellulose component before testing, but since this can reduce the volume of the sample to 20% of its original size, testing of the whole wood is often performed as well. Charcoal is often tested but is likely to need treatment to remove contaminants.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_27-30_49-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_27-30-49">\n          [43]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AitkenWashing_50-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-AitkenWashing-50">\n          [44]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Unburnt bone can be tested; it is usual to date it using\n        <a href="/wiki/Collagen" title="Collagen">\n         collagen\n        </a>\n        , the protein fraction that remains after washing away the bone\'s structural material.\n        <a href="/wiki/Hydroxyproline" title="Hydroxyproline">\n         Hydroxyproline\n        </a>\n        , one of the constituent amino acids in bone, was once thought to be a reliable indicator as it was not known to occur except in bone, but it has since been detected in groundwater.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_27-30_49-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_27-30-49">\n          [43]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        For burnt bone, testability depends on the conditions under which the bone was burnt. If the bone was heated under\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reducing_conditions" title="Reducing conditions">\n         reducing conditions\n        </a>\n        , it (and associated organic matter) may have been carbonized. In this case the sample is often usable.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_27-30_49-4">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_27-30-49">\n          [43]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Shells from both marine and land organisms consist almost entirely of calcium carbonate, either as\n        <a href="/wiki/Aragonite" title="Aragonite">\n         aragonite\n        </a>\n        or as\n        <a href="/wiki/Calcite" title="Calcite">\n         calcite\n        </a>\n        , or some mixture of the two. Calcium carbonate is very susceptible to dissolving and recrystallizing; the recrystallized material will contain carbon from the sample\'s environment, which may be of geological origin. If testing recrystallized shell is unavoidable, it is sometimes possible to identify the original shell material from a sequence of tests.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n         <a href="#cite_note-51">\n          [45]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        It is also possible to test\n        <a href="/wiki/Conchiolin" title="Conchiolin">\n         conchiolin\n        </a>\n        , an organic protein found in shell, but it constitutes only 1\xe2\x80\x932% of shell material.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AitkenWashing_50-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-AitkenWashing-50">\n          [44]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The three major components of peat are humic acid,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humins" title="Humins">\n         humins\n        </a>\n        , and fulvic acid. Of these, humins give the most reliable date as they are insoluble in alkali and less likely to contain contaminants from the sample\'s environment.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AitkenWashing_50-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-AitkenWashing-50">\n          [44]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        A particular difficulty with dried peat is the removal of rootlets, which are likely to be hard to distinguish from the sample material.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_27-30_49-5">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Bowman_27-30-49">\n          [43]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Soil contains organic material, but because of the likelihood of contamination by humic acid of more recent origin, it is very difficult to get satisfactory radiocarbon dates. It is preferable to sieve the soil for fragments of organic origin, and date the fragments with methods that are tolerant of small sample sizes.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AitkenWashing_50-4">\n         <a href="#cite_note-AitkenWashing-50">\n          [44]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Other materials that have been successfully dated include ivory, paper, textiles, individual seeds and grains, straw from within mud bricks, and charred food remains found in pottery.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AitkenWashing_50-5">\n         <a href="#cite_note-AitkenWashing-50">\n          [44]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Preparation_and_size">\n        Preparation and size\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Preparation and size">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Particularly for older samples, it may be useful to enrich the amount of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in the sample before testing. This can be done with a thermal diffusion column. The process takes about a month and requires a sample about ten times as large as would be needed otherwise, but it allows more precise measurement of the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio in old material and extends the maximum age that can be reliably reported.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Once contamination has been removed, samples must be converted to a form suitable for the measuring technology to be used.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BowmanMeasure_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BowmanMeasure-53">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Where gas is required,\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       is widely used.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BowmanMeasure_53-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BowmanMeasure-53">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_76-78_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_76-78-54">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For samples to be used in\n       <a href="/wiki/Liquid_scintillation_counting" title="Liquid scintillation counting">\n        liquid scintillation counters\n       </a>\n       , the carbon must be in liquid form; the sample is typically converted to\n       <a href="/wiki/Benzene" title="Benzene">\n        benzene\n       </a>\n       . For\n       <a href="/wiki/Accelerator_mass_spectrometry" title="Accelerator mass spectrometry">\n        accelerator mass spectrometry\n       </a>\n       , solid graphite targets are the most common, although\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_carbide" title="Iron carbide">\n        iron carbide\n       </a>\n       and gaseous\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        CO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       can also be used.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BowmanMeasure_53-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BowmanMeasure-53">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trumbore96_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Trumbore96-55">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The quantity of material needed for testing depends on the sample type and the technology being used. There are two types of testing technology: detectors that record radioactivity, known as beta counters, and accelerator mass spectrometers. For beta counters, a sample weighing at least 10 grams (0.35 ounces) is typically required.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BowmanMeasure_53-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BowmanMeasure-53">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Accelerator mass spectrometry (AMS) is much more sensitive, and samples as small as 0.5 milligrams (0.0077 grains) can be used.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Measurement_and_results">\n        Measurement and results\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Measurement and results">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1_MV_accelerator_mass_spectrometer.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="530" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1_MV_accelerator_mass_spectrometer.jpg/220px-1_MV_accelerator_mass_spectrometer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1_MV_accelerator_mass_spectrometer.jpg/330px-1_MV_accelerator_mass_spectrometer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/1_MV_accelerator_mass_spectrometer.jpg/440px-1_MV_accelerator_mass_spectrometer.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1_MV_accelerator_mass_spectrometer.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Measuring\n         <span class="chemf nowrap">\n          <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n           14\n           <br/>\n          </span>\n          C\n         </span>\n         is now most commonly done with an accelerator mass spectrometer\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       For decades after Libby performed the first radiocarbon dating experiments, the only way to measure the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in a sample was to detect the radioactive decay of individual carbon atoms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BowmanMeasure_53-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BowmanMeasure-53">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In this approach, what is measured is the activity, in number of decay events per unit mass per time period, of the sample.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_76-78_54-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_76-78-54">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This method is also known as "beta counting", because it is the beta particles emitted by the decaying\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       atoms that are detected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the late 1970s an alternative approach became available: directly counting the number of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       atoms in a given sample, via accelerator mass spectrometry, usually referred to as AMS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BowmanMeasure_53-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BowmanMeasure-53">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       AMS counts the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio directly, instead of the activity of the sample, but measurements of activity and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio can be converted into each other exactly.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_76-78_54-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_76-78-54">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For some time, beta counting methods were more accurate than AMS, but as of 2014 AMS is more accurate and has become the method of choice for radiocarbon measurements.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:14_58-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:14-58">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition to improved accuracy, AMS has two further significant advantages over beta counting: it can perform accurate testing on samples much too small for beta counting; and it is much faster\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 an accuracy of 1% can be achieved in minutes with AMS, which is far quicker than would be achievable with the older technology.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Beta_counting">\n        Beta counting\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Beta counting">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Libby\'s first detector was a\n       <a href="/wiki/Geiger_counter" title="Geiger counter">\n        Geiger counter\n       </a>\n       of his own design. He converted the carbon in his sample to lamp black (soot) and coated the inner surface of a cylinder with it. This cylinder was inserted into the counter in such a way that the counting wire was inside the sample cylinder, in order that there should be no material between the sample and the wire.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BowmanMeasure_53-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BowmanMeasure-53">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Any interposing material would have interfered with the detection of radioactivity, since the beta particles emitted by decaying\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       are so weak that half are stopped by a 0.01\xc2\xa0mm thickness of aluminium.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_76-78_54-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_76-78-54">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Libby\'s method was soon superseded by gas\n       <a href="/wiki/Proportional_counter" title="Proportional counter">\n        proportional counters\n       </a>\n       , which were less affected by bomb carbon (the additional\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       created by nuclear weapons testing). These counters record bursts of ionization caused by the beta particles emitted by the decaying\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       atoms; the bursts are proportional to the energy of the particle, so other sources of ionization, such as background radiation, can be identified and ignored. The counters are surrounded by lead or steel shielding, to eliminate background radiation and to reduce the incidence of cosmic rays. In addition,\n       <a href="/wiki/Electronic_anticoincidence" title="Electronic anticoincidence">\n        anticoincidence\n       </a>\n       detectors are used; these record events outside the counter, and any event recorded simultaneously both inside and outside the counter is regarded as an extraneous event and ignored.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aitken_76-78_54-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aitken_76-78-54">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The other common technology used for measuring\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       activity is liquid scintillation counting, which was invented in 1950, but which had to wait until the early 1960s, when efficient methods of benzene synthesis were developed, to become competitive with gas counting; after 1970 liquid counters became the more common technology choice for newly constructed dating laboratories. The counters work by detecting flashes of light caused by the beta particles emitted by\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       as they interact with a fluorescing agent added to the benzene. Like gas counters, liquid scintillation counters require shielding and anticoincidence counters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For both the gas proportional counter and liquid scintillation counter, what is measured is the number of beta particles detected in a given time period. Since the mass of the sample is known, this can be converted to a standard measure of activity in units of either counts per minute per gram of carbon (cpm/g C), or\n       <a href="/wiki/Becquerel" title="Becquerel">\n        becquerels\n       </a>\n       per kg (Bq/kg C, in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI_units" title="SI units">\n        SI units\n       </a>\n       ). Each measuring device is also used to measure the activity of a blank sample\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 a sample prepared from carbon old enough to have no activity. This provides a value for the background radiation, which must be subtracted from the measured activity of the sample being dated to get the activity attributable solely to that sample\'s\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       . In addition, a sample with a standard activity is measured, to provide a baseline for comparison.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:10-63">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Accelerator_mass_spectrometry">\n        Accelerator mass spectrometry\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Accelerator mass spectrometry">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Accelerator_mass_spectrometer_schematic_for_radiocarbon.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="224" data-file-width="605" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Accelerator_mass_spectrometer_schematic_for_radiocarbon.svg/400px-Accelerator_mass_spectrometer_schematic_for_radiocarbon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Accelerator_mass_spectrometer_schematic_for_radiocarbon.svg/600px-Accelerator_mass_spectrometer_schematic_for_radiocarbon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Accelerator_mass_spectrometer_schematic_for_radiocarbon.svg/800px-Accelerator_mass_spectrometer_schematic_for_radiocarbon.svg.png 2x" width="400"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Accelerator_mass_spectrometer_schematic_for_radiocarbon.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Simplified schematic layout of an accelerator mass spectrometer used for counting carbon isotopes for carbon dating\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       AMS counts the atoms of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       in a given sample, determining the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ratio directly. The sample, often in the form of graphite, is made to emit C\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x92\n       </sup>\n       ions (carbon atoms with a single negative charge), which are injected into an\n       <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">\n        accelerator\n       </a>\n       . The ions are accelerated and passed through a stripper, which removes several electrons so that the ions emerge with a positive charge. The C\n       <sup>\n        3+\n       </sup>\n       ions are then passed through a magnet that curves their path; the heavier ions are curved less than the lighter ones, so the different isotopes emerge as separate streams of ions. A particle detector then records the number of ions detected in the\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       stream, but since the volume of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       (and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , needed for calibration) is too great for individual ion detection, counts are determined by measuring the electric current created in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Faraday_cup" title="Faraday cup">\n        Faraday cup\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:9-64">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some AMS facilities are also able to evaluate a sample\'s fractionation, another piece of data necessary for calculating the sample\'s radiocarbon age.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The use of AMS, as opposed to simpler forms of mass spectrometry, is necessary because of the need to distinguish the carbon isotopes from other atoms or molecules that are very close in mass, such as\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        N\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        CH\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BowmanMeasure_53-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BowmanMeasure-53">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As with beta counting, both blank samples and standard samples are used.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_64-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:9-64">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Two different kinds of blank may be measured: a sample of dead carbon that has undergone no chemical processing, to detect any machine background, and a sample known as a process blank made from dead carbon that is processed into target material in exactly the same way as the sample which is being dated. Any\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       signal from the machine background blank is likely to be caused either by beams of ions that have not followed the expected path inside the detector, or by carbon hydrides such as\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        CH\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       or\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        CH\n       </span>\n       . A\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       signal from the process blank measures the amount of contamination introduced during the preparation of the sample. These measurements are used in the subsequent calculation of the age of the sample.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:11-66">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Calculations">\n        Calculations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radiocarbon_dating&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Calculations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Calculation_of_radiocarbon_dates" title="Calculation of radiocarbon dates">\n        Calculation of radiocarbon dates\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The calculations to be performed on the measurements taken depend on the technology used, since beta counters measure the sample\'s radioactivity whereas AMS determines the ratio of the three different carbon isotopes in the sample.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_66-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:11-66">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       To determine the age of a sample whose activity has been measured by beta counting, the ratio of its activity to the activity of the standard must be found. To determine this, a blank sample (of old, or dead, carbon) is measured, and a sample of known activity is measured. The additional samples allow errors such as background radiation and systematic errors in the laboratory setup to be detected and corrected for.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_63-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:10-63">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The most common standard sample material is oxalic acid, such as the HOxII standard, 1,000\xc2\xa0lb of which was prepared by NIST in 1977 from French beet harvests.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The results from AMS testing are in the form of ratios of\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         12\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         13\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.5em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         14\n         <br/>\n        </span>\n        C\n       </span>\n       , which are used to calculate Fm, the "fraction modern".
